### Run 2 generated — stdin protocol parse-error recovery contract (2026-04-17T15:25:55Z)

- [x] stdin-protocol-parse-error-recovery-contract: The stdin listener thread at `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs#start_stdin_listener` is the single-threaded choke point through which EVERY external automation command reaches the app. A panic, `break`, or `return` anywhere inside its line-processing loop permanently severs the automation surface until the app restarts — and because the dev-watch session's forwarder still accepts writes to the pipe with no error, the failure mode is silent: every subsequent `session.sh send` / `rpc` returns success while the app ignores the payload. The most likely cause of such a severance is a "clean up" refactor of the parse-error or oversized-line arm — replacing `Err(e) => { warn(...); }` (fall-through) with `Err(e) => return Err(e)` or `Err(_) => break` "to propagate errors cleanly." Acceptance: (a) Live verify on dev-watch that the listener survives 3 distinct malformed-payload shapes and continues to dispatch a valid command after each — `{"malformed":"..."}` (missing field `type`) → `stdin_parse_failed` logged, loop continues; plain text `this is not even json at all` → `stdin_parse_failed` (expected ident), loop continues; `{"type":"unknownCommandType",...}` → `stdin_parse_failed` (unknown variant), loop continues; then a valid `listAutomationWindows` parses + dispatches + returns a response. (b) Source-level contract at `tests/stdin_parse_error_recovery_contract.rs`: (1) the parse-error arm body contains `stdin_parse_failed` (observability gate) AND NONE of `break`, `return`, `panic!(`, `unreachable!(`, `todo!(` (any of these would kill the listener); (2) the `Ok(StdinLineRead::TooLong { raw, raw_len })` arm body contains `stdin_command_too_large` AND NONE of the same forbidden control-flow tokens — a 20 KiB malformed script payload must not brick the listener; (3) positive counter-assertion that the OUTER `Err(e) => { ... break; }` read-error arm DOES contain `break;` within 400 bytes of its `stdin_read_error` anchor — without this break, a broken-pipe EOF would busy-spin. Uses a brace-counted `start_stdin_listener_body()` + `balanced_block_body()` + `parse_error_arm_body()` + `too_long_arm_body()` helpers to scope each assertion to the exact arm body, so matches elsewhere in the listener body don't cause false positives or negatives. *(Pass #56 Run 2: shipped. Live verification on dev-watch pid 38095 — 3 malformed payloads each logged `stdin_parse_failed` with a distinct reason (`missing field 'type'`, `expected ident`, `unknown variant 'unknownCommandType'`), and a follow-up `listAutomationWindows` returned a valid response proving the loop survived. 3-test contract at `tests/stdin_parse_error_recovery_contract.rs` passes 3/3 in 0.00s after 2.89s compile. No production code edited — the listener's resilience is already correct by construction (the parse-error and TooLong arms fall through; only the outer read-error arm breaks); this pass pins the structural conditions so a future refactor that replaced the fall-through with `break` / `return` / `panic!` trips CI before reaching a user. The `too_long_arm_body` helper is intentionally split: it first locates the `"Ok(StdinLineRead::TooLong {"` anchor, then scans for `=> {` after that point, because `balanced_block_body`'s naive `find('{')` would otherwise lock onto the destructure pattern's opening brace inside `{ raw, raw_len }`. The third test is the inverse of the first two — the outer IO-level read-error arm MUST `break;` because continuing to loop on EOF/broken-pipe busy-spins forever. Coverage 65 → 66.)*

### Run 2 generated — triggerBuiltin repeat-idempotency contract (2026-04-17T12:44:00Z)

- [x] trigger-builtin-repeat-idempotency: Repeat invocations of the same `triggerBuiltin X` — whether back-to-back, rapid-fire, or interleaved with a lighter command — must produce identical view + automation-registry state. Scripts can legitimately fire the same builtin twice (user double-presses a hotkey; a watcher fires twice; retry-on-timeout logic in the script harness), and state must not drift. Pass #52 pinned that the post-match `update_automation_semantic_surface` is a pure overwrite (so the surface tag can't drift), but nothing pins that the ARM bodies themselves are structurally idempotent — a refactor that, say, pushed a duplicate entry into an automation Vec from the `tab-ai` arm would accumulate N registry entries after N trigger calls. Acceptance: (a) Live receipts on dev-watch — `triggerBuiltin tab-ai` ×2 back-to-back produces identical `listAutomationWindows` (1 main window, `semanticSurface:"acpChat"`, same bounds) on both calls; `triggerBuiltin clipboard-history` ×2 produces identical `getState` (`promptType:"clipboardHistory"`, `choiceCount:100`, same `selectedIndex`); `triggerBuiltin emoji` ×3 rapid-fire (200 ms apart) still leaves exactly 1 main window with `semanticSurface:"emojiPicker"`. (b) Source-level contract at `tests/trigger_builtin_repeat_idempotency_contract.rs`: (1) no `ExternalCommand::TriggerBuiltin` arm body directly calls `upsert_automation_window(` or `remove_automation_window(` — registry lifecycle must flow through view-state transitions, not per-trigger side effects; (2) no arm body has `.push(` or `.insert(` co-located with `automation_windows` — defense-in-depth against bypassing the named registry APIs; (3) every `view.current_view =` assignment in an arm body is unconditional (not guarded by `view.current_view !=`/`==`) — a skip-guard would make repeat triggers non-idempotent in a subtle way (second call skips both the assignment and any side effects it would have unlocked). Uses brace-counted span extraction to scope all checks to the `ExternalCommand::TriggerBuiltin { ref name } => { ... }` arm body only, ignoring matches elsewhere in the dispatcher. *(Pass #55 Run 2: shipped. Live verification on dev-watch pid 38095 — three repeat scenarios all produced identical state: `triggerBuiltin tab-ai` ×2 → `semanticSurface:"acpChat"` + `windows.length==1` both times; `triggerBuiltin clipboard-history` ×2 → `promptType:"clipboardHistory"` + `choiceCount:100` both times; `triggerBuiltin emoji` ×3 rapid-fire → `semanticSurface:"emojiPicker"` + `windows.length==1`. 3-test contract at `tests/trigger_builtin_repeat_idempotency_contract.rs` passes 3/3 in 0.00s after 17.14s first-compile. Complements Pass #52 (post-match re-key unconditional + pure-overwrite), Pass #53 (`_ =>` arm side-effect-free), Pass #54 (case-insensitive dispatch), Pass #42 (arm-heads/map entries symmetric). ### Run 2 generated — triggerBuiltin unknown-name preserves surface tag (2026-04-17T12:32:00Z)

### Run 2 generated — detached popup concurrent close safety (2026-04-17T11:52:00Z)

- [x] detached-popup-concurrent-close-safety: Pass #47 flagged this as a candidate follow-up. The detached ACP popup has THREE cleanup sites against the single `CHAT_WINDOW: OnceLock<Mutex<Option<ChatWindowState>>>` static — (a) the placeholder `on_window_should_close` in `chat_window_options`, (b) the thread-carrying `on_window_should_close` in `open_chat_window_with_thread`, and (c) the external-caller `close_chat_window` helper. Rust-level mutual exclusion is guaranteed because all three lock the SAME Mutex, but the exactly-once FUNCTIONAL guarantee — that `remove_runtime_window_handle` / `remove_automation_window` are not double-run on the same id — depends on every site using the `slot.lock() + g.take()` pattern: the winner of the race observes `Some(state)` and does the work, the loser observes `None` and no-ops. A drive-by refactor that replaced `.take()` with `.as_ref().cloned()` or `.clone()` (e.g. "cloning feels safer") would silently break this: both paths could observe the same state and double-run the cleanup pair, corrupting the automation registry. Pin the invariant at source level: (a) `g.take()` must appear at least 3 times in `src/ai/acp/chat_window.rs` (one per close site); (b) the `CHAT_WINDOW` static is declared exactly once and initialized at each close site via `get_or_init(|| Mutex::new(None))` (≥3 occurrences); (c) no clone-out-of-mutex patterns (`g.as_ref().cloned()`, ` g.clone()`, `(*g).clone()`) appear anywhere in the file. *(Pass #48 Run 2: shipped. New `tests/detached_acp_concurrent_close_safety_contract.rs` with 3 tests: (1) `every_close_site_takes_state_out_of_the_mutex` — counts `g.take()` occurrences, asserts ≥3 (matches current actual count: placeholder on_close line 124, thread on_close line 193, close_chat_window line 528); (2) `close_sites_use_the_same_chat_window_mutex` — asserts the static declaration appears exactly once AND `CHAT_WINDOW.get_or_init(|| Mutex::new(None))` appears ≥3 times (prevents a second static forking the mutex); (3) `no_close_site_uses_non_take_extraction` — forbids ` g.as_ref().cloned()`, ` g.clone()`, ` (*g).clone()` (whitespace-anchored to avoid false-positive on `dialog.clone()`, `config.clone()`, etc. — the first draft failed this test because the unanchored `g.clone()` pattern matched `dialog.clone()` at line 743). All 3 tests pass in 0.00s after a 17.88s first-compile. ### Run 2 generated — detached popup close cleanup contract (2026-04-17T11:40:00Z)

- [x] detached-popup-close-cleanup-contract: Pin Pass #29's registry-leak fix at source level. The detached ACP window has TWO close paths — (a) user titlebar close / `Cmd+W` routed through the `on_window_should_close` callback registered inside `open_chat_window_with_thread`, and (b) external callers invoking `close_chat_window(cx)` directly (e.g. `TriggerAction host=acpDetached action_id=acp_close` from Pass #29's dispatcher). Pass #29 added the `remove_runtime_window_handle(id)` + `remove_automation_window(id)` adjacent pair inside `close_chat_window` specifically because the helper `take()`s `CHAT_WINDOW.slot` BEFORE calling `window.remove_window()`, which means the on_window_should_close callback later finds the slot drained (`g.take()` returns `None`) and silently skips its own cleanup branch. A mechanical refactor that "simplifies" `close_chat_window` to delegate back to `window.remove_window()` and let on_window_should_close handle cleanup would silently regress the leak — the bug lives in the INTERACTION between the two paths, not either one locally. Pin both sites. Acceptance: (1) `close_chat_window` body contains the adjacent `remove_runtime_window_handle(id)` + `remove_automation_window(id)` pair, gated by `if let Some(ref id) = state.automation_id`, appearing BEFORE `window.remove_window();` in the function body, with `save_window_from_gpui(WindowRole::AcpChat, ...)` persistence intact; (2) the whole file carries the adjacent pair in at least two sites; (3) every `remove_automation_window(id)` call is paired with an adjacent `remove_runtime_window_handle(id)` so neither half can be orphaned. *(Pass #47 Run 2: shipped. New `tests/detached_acp_close_cleanup_contract.rs` with 2 tests + 2 helpers (`close_chat_window_body` slicer that slices from the fn header to the next top-level `\npub fn ` or `\nfn `; `count_adjacent_cleanup_pairs` whole-file scanner using a 160-byte sliding window after each `remove_runtime_window_handle(id)` occurrence). Adjacency matcher accepts only whitespace, `;`, and the module-qualified prefix `crate::windows::` between the two calls — any other logic wedged between them fails the check. Bug in first draft: the `body.find("window.remove_window()")` search was matching the DOC COMMENT at line 533 before the actual call at line 554, so the "pair before remove_window" assertion looked at comment bytes; fixed by searching for the trailing semicolon form `window.remove_window();` which appears only at the real call site. Both tests pass in 0.00s after 19.50s first-compile. Documented the two-path invariant in `lat.md/acp-chat.md` as a new subsection `### Close cleanup — both paths drain the registry pair` under `## Detached window behavior`, enumerating the two entry paths and their distinct sequencing, and cross-referencing the new contract test. `cargo fmt --check` clean; `lat check` clean. Complements Pass #46's supplier-side pin (`detached_acp_popup_registry_surface_contract.rs`) and Pass #29's dispatcher-side routing (`trigger_action_acp_detached_host_contract.rs`) — the three contracts together cover creation (Pass #46), external dispatch (Pass #29), and close cleanup (Pass #47) of the detached-popup lifecycle.)*

### Run 2 generated — hide-path asymmetry contract (2026-04-17T11:20:00Z)

### Run 2 generated — direct subview→subview flip integrity (2026-04-17T11:14:00Z)

- [x] direct-subview-to-subview-trigger-surface-rekey: Passes #42 and #43 verified the semantic-surface contract by always firing `triggerBuiltin X` from a scriptList baseline and confirming the re-key; then `hide` reset to scriptList before the next trigger. Real automation workflows won't always reset between triggers — scripts can chain `triggerBuiltin A` → `triggerBuiltin B` directly. No source changes needed — the dispatcher's post-match `update_automation_semantic_surface("main", semantic_surface_for_main_view(&view.current_view))` call fires unconditionally, so the re-key is pure-overwrite by construction; this is a dynamic-behavior verification pass. The existing Pass #42 symmetry contract at `tests/dispatcher_semantic_surface_symmetry_contract.rs` already pins the three static layers; adding a source-level test for direct-flip dynamics would be structurally redundant since the guarantee is "the re-key is unconditional," which is already encoded by the fact that ALL match arms flow into a single post-match re-key call with no intermediate branch. Adds live confidence that the contract holds under sequential-trigger workloads.)*

The stored identity is the BARE filename (no dir) returned by `build_tab_ai_screenshot_filename` — already encodes three independent axes (timestamp + PID + sequence) per `tests/screenshot_identity_threading_contract.rs`. Main-window `getState` arm at `src/prompt_handler/mod.rs:2622` reads through the accessor; the secondary-window and target-error paths correctly pass `None` (their state snapshots are not main's capture state). Story text's original premise (`promptType="imagePrompt"` + `imageIdentity=screenshot:<timestamp>`) was fundamentally wrong — screenshots don't flip prompt-type, they are staged into the AI input. New contract captures the real identity-threading invariant via `screenshotIdentity` which automation can read directly instead of grepping the filesystem. Pinned by `tests/state_result_screenshot_identity_contract.rs` (4 tests, all passing): (1) variant declares field with camelCase rename + skip_if_none, (2) constructor accepts as trailing param + forwards into struct literal, (3) both capture paths call `record_last_screenshot_identity(filename.clone())` in the right order, (4) prompt_handler main path reads through the accessor. After entering ACP chat via `triggerBuiltin tab-ai` then issuing `{type:"hide"}`, `listAutomationWindows` still reports `{id:"ai", kind:"ai", title:"Script Kit AI", visible:true, semanticSurface:"acpChat", parentWindowId:"main", parentKind:"main"}` as a second window entry — even though `getState` reports `windowVisible:false, promptType:"none"` and main's own entry has been correctly re-keyed to `semanticSurface:"scriptList"`. Result: agentic callers using `{type:"kind",kind:"ai"}` targeting post-hide see a stale entry whose `visible:true` bit disagrees with main's visibility state, and whose `semanticSurface:"acpChat"` bit disagrees with main's actual view (now scriptList). Evidence (pid 19829, fresh binary from Pass #18, actions A22-A33): (1) **Rapid-fire** A06-A15 — 10× `listAutomationWindows` after `triggerBuiltin tab-ai` → consistent 2-window result (`main`+`ai`), no flapping; (2) **Boundary** A23-A25 — `getAcpState` with nonexistent id / unavailable kind (`acpDetached`) / no-match `titleContains` → all returned `status:"ok"` with clean `warnings:["target_unsupported: ..."]`; no crash, no wrong receipt; (3) **Composition** A26-A29 — `hide` → `getState` shows `{windowVisible:false, promptType:"none"}` ✓ but `listAutomationWindows` STILL shows `ai` entry with `visible:true, semanticSurface:"acpChat"` ❌ (the anomaly); `show` → main re-surfaces as scriptList but `ai` entry persists unchanged; (4) **Interleaved** A30-A33 — re-entering via `triggerBuiltin tab-ai` does NOT duplicate the entry (single `ai` row, not two) because `ensure_embedded_ai_window(true)` upserts on fixed id `"ai"`; subsequent `hide` reproduces the stale-entry state. Refactor threat: the three-way symmetry (4 entries + 1 close-flow exit + 1 hide-flow exit) is not source-pinned — a future refactor that consolidates the 4 entry sites into a helper (the Pass #17 Fix's next-step (a) flagged this possibility) could easily drop the hide-flow teardown because it lives in a different module. Filing as `[?]` rather than `[!]`: the bug does not break any currently-shipping agentic flow (all Run 3-9 getAcpState/listAcpTurns passes correctly resolve through the registry), but it does violate the listAutomationWindows "registry ≈ reality" contract implied by Pass #18's receipt-fidelity Fix. - [x] session-send-await-parse-sad-path-concurrent-cross-correlation: Run 5 Pass #13 fix landed via option (b) from the filing's menu — a lenient pre-deserialization requestId extract in Rust so the `stdin_parse_failed` tracing span carries `correlation_id = "stdin:req:<request_id>"` symmetrically with the happy path. The new `pub(crate) fn extract_request_id_lenient(line: &str) -> Option<String>` in `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs` mirrors the session.sh sed pattern (`sed -nE 's/.*"requestId"[[:space:]]*:[[:space:]]*"([^"]*)".*/\1/p'`) and charset regex (`^[A-Za-z0-9_.:/-]+$`) exactly. The `Err(e)` arm of `start_stdin_listener` now formats `stdin:req:<id>` when the lenient extract succeeds, falling back to `stdin:parse:<uuid>` for payloads where the `"requestId":"..."` structure is itself broken. The shell-side `cmd_send` sad-path grep is now scoped on `cid=stdin:req:${req_id}` just like the happy-path grep, with the legacy unscoped grep preserved as the req_id-empty fallback. - [x] stdin-setfilter-inputvalue-unbounded: Run 8 Pass #23 (2026-04-19T01:37Z) — **CLOSED by Prompt: Pin** (option (b) from the acceptance menu: document the no-bound contract explicitly, pin the 16 KiB stdin line cap as the sole gate). Decision rationale: option (a) (4 KiB soft cap) would silently change callers that pass long filters and race the MAX-bytes stdin line cap anyway; option (c) (reject at ingest) breaks existing automation that intentionally uses longer filters for zero-match verification. Live verification against session pid 855: `setFilter text:"aaa"` → `getState.inputValue:"aaa" len:3` ✓; `setFilter text:<2000 'x'>` → `getState.inputValue len:2000 all_x:True` ✓ (verbatim, no truncation marker, no length warning — exactly as documented). Refactor threat defended: a well-meaning contributor adds a "safety" cap at the setFilter writer or getState reader, thinking it defends against large payloads, when the stdin line cap already bounds the path. The pin's negative assertion ("no `.truncate(` between signature and store") catches this shape-class directly. Original `[?]` prose preserved below. --- Pass #8 Run 4 attacker probe — a 10 000-char `setFilter.text` yields a 10 000-char `getState.inputValue` in the RPC receipt with no truncation or `inputValueTruncated` marker. Not a crash or silent corruption; the match engine correctly returns `choiceCount=0` for the unmatched long input. Concern: `getState` responses can grow without bound with user-controlled input, and the session stdin pipe has finite buffers. Design decision needed: document the contract ("inputValue echoes user input verbatim, callers MUST handle arbitrary size"), add a soft cap (e.g. truncate at 4KB with `inputValueTruncated:true` flag), or constrain at ingest (reject `setFilter.text` longer than N chars). Acceptance once resolved: either `getState.inputValue.length` is bounded, or the protocol docs explicitly state no bound and the cap is the stdin pipe's 16KB `MAX_STDIN_COMMAND_BYTES`.

- [x] session-send-await-parse-concurrent-cross-correlation: Run 5 Pass #10 fix landed — ZERO Rust changes needed. Investigation revealed `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs::start_stdin_listener` already emits `correlation_id = "stdin:req:<request_id>"` (format `cid=stdin:req:<request_id>` in app.log) via `tracing::info!(correlation_id = %correlation_id)` whenever the parsed command carries a requestId. The fix is entirely shell-side: `scripts/agentic/session.sh` `cmd_send` now extracts `requestId` from the sent payload via `sed -nE 's/.*"requestId"[[:space:]]*:[[:space:]]*"([^"]*)".*/\1/p'`, validates it against the conservative charset `^[A-Za-z0-9_.:/-]+$` (to defend the grep from attacker-controlled injection via shell/grep metachars or whitespace), and scopes the happy-path grep to `grep -F -- "cid=stdin:req:${req_id} " | grep -m1 'event_type=stdin_command_parsed'`. Trailing space in the grep pattern prevents prefix matches (e.g. `p10-F-1` vs `p10-F-10`). Live smoke test: Pass #8 Phase F replayed with 5 concurrent sends of `getState, hide, show, getState, hide` now returns each send's correct commandType (getState/hide/show/getState/hide) instead of all five reporting `show`. Sends without a requestId OR with one containing shell/grep metachars fall back to legacy offset-first grep (single-caller serial-usage precondition). Sad-path (parseError) correlation remains offset-first because parse failure precedes requestId extraction — that race surface is narrower but still exists for concurrent parse failures; not a blocker because Pass #8 Phase F observed zero concurrent parse failures. Contract pinned by `tests/session_send_await_parse_contract.rs::cmd_send_scopes_happy_path_grep_on_request_id` (+1, total 6/6 green). Lat doc update: `lat.md/automation.md` §"Session send parse receipts" now documents the request-id scoping, the charset guard, and the sad-path remaining race.

- [x] tool-rpc-preempt-parse-failure-await: Run 8 Pass #17 (2026-04-19T00:36Z) — **ADD**. Shipped preemptive `stdin_parse_failed` detection inside `scripts/agentic/await-response.ts`'s existing `while (Date.now() < deadline)` poll loop. New helper `scanForParseFailure(logPath, requestId, startOffset)` reads the app.log tail from `parseFailScanOffset`, filters lines on `cidMarker = \`cid=stdin:req:${requestId} \`` (trailing space preventing prefix matches per session.sh cmd_rpc line ~599), requires `"event_type=stdin_parse_failed"` literal, extracts the `error=` suffix, strips serde's ` at line N column M` tail via regex, and truncates at `ERROR_MSG_MAX_CHARS = 200` to mirror session.sh's `cut -c1-200` bound. Gated on `charsetSafeRequestId = REQUEST_ID_CHARSET.test(requestId)` (`^[A-Za-z0-9_.:/-]+$` — identical to Rust `extract_request_id_lenient` and shell `cmd_rpc` line ~598); charset-unsafe ids route to Rust's `cid=stdin:parse:<uuid>` which the scoped grep cannot match and fall through to the shell post-hoc unscoped-grep fallback (session.sh lines ~600-602). Preempt block runs BEFORE `scanLog(...)` within each iteration — fast-fail path wastes no POLL_INTERVAL (~50ms) of latency. Exit code 3 (`PARSE_ERROR_EXIT_CODE`) is new stable contract for "parse error surfaced preemptively" (distinct from exit 1 generic timeout and exit 2 infrastructure error). Envelope shape symmetric with session.sh cmd_rpc's post-hoc emission: `errorResult(sessionName, requestId, "parse_error", errMsg)`. Live receipts this pass: A1 charset-safe malformed `{"type":"setFilter","value":"foo","requestId":"p17-preempt-v1"}` → `{"code":"parse_error","message":"automation_payload_mismatch: \"setFilter\" is a known automation verb but the payload did not validate: unknown field \`value\`, expected \`text\` or \`requestId\`"}` in **38ms** (vs pre-fix 5000ms full `--timeout` wait — ~130× speedup). A2 positive control `{"type":"getState","requestId":"p17-positive-v1"}` → `status:ok` in 32ms (preempt correctly returns null, typed scan picks up `stateResult`). A3 charset-unsafe `{"type":"bogusVerbA3","requestId":"p17-charset+unsafe"}` → `parse_error` in 3092ms via shell post-hoc unscoped-grep fallback (preemptive correctly skipped because charset check fails — Pass #12 fallback path still operational). Contract pinned by `tests/agentic_await_response_preempt_parse_failure_contract.rs` (7 source-grep tests — exit code constant, charset gate, scoped cid marker with trailing space, event_type literal match, error-length cap + suffix strip, preempt-before-typed-scan ordering, `parse_error` code emission). `lat.md/automation.md` §"Session send parse receipts" updated: "future extension" language replaced with stable-contract description citing the 7-test anchor and exit code 3. Falsifier: any commit that drops `const PARSE_ERROR_EXIT_CODE = 3`, removes the `if (charsetSafeRequestId)` guard, reverses the preempt-vs-typed-scan order within the poll loop, or changes the envelope code to anything other than `"parse_error"` would revert the 38ms fast-fail back toward 5000ms and break one or more of the 7 contract assertions.

- [x] cmd-rpc-scan-misses-requestid-charset-boundary: Run 8 Pass #12 (2026-04-19T02:07Z) — **CLOSED by Prompt: Fix**. Adopted preferred option (a) from the fix menu — mirrored `cmd_send`'s line-390 charset gate into `cmd_rpc`'s post-hoc parse-failure scan at `scripts/agentic/session.sh` lines ~582-601. When `request_id` matches `^[A-Za-z0-9_.:/-]+$` the existing scoped grep `grep -F -- "cid=stdin:req:${request_id} "` runs unchanged; when the charset check fails (e.g. requestId `a+b`, `a\b`), the scan falls back to unscoped `grep -m1 'event_type=stdin_parse_failed'` on the same `tail -c "$tail_bytes" "$log_path"` byte window — restoring parse-error surfacing for attacker-probe requestIds at the cost of cross-concurrent-call de-interleaving (the same trade `cmd_send` makes on lines 390-392, 408-410, 438-440). Rejected (b) broaden-charset (expands attack surface) and (c) Rust-always-emits-stdin:req (drops Pass #13's shell-metachar defense). All 6 tests in the contract file green (11.61s compile + 0.00s run). `lat.md/automation.md` §"Session send parse receipts" updated: bumped `cmd_rpc` test count from 5 to 6 and documented the charset fallback as stable contract. Original `[?]` finding preserved below. --- Run 5 Pass #16 attacker probe (2026-04-18T10:34:16Z) — `scripts/agentic/session.sh` `cmd_rpc` post-hoc parse-error scan (shipped Pass #15) silently fails when the caller's `requestId` contains any character outside the conservative charset `[A-Za-z0-9_.:/-]`. Reproducers (21-action, 5-category probe output at `/tmp/probe-run5-pass16/`): A3 `{"type":"bogusVerbA3","requestId":"a+b"}` → returns `{"code":"timeout","message":"No response matching requestId 'a+b' and type 'elementsResult' within 2000ms"}` even though app.log has `cid=stdin:parse:957b5c43-… event_type=stdin_parse_failed payload_summary={type:bogusVerbA3,…} error=unknown variant \`bogusVerbA3\`…`. A5 `{"type":"bogusVerbA5","requestId":"a\\b"}` (backslash) shows identical class with `cid=stdin:parse:785f19da-…`. Root cause: Rust `extract_request_id_lenient` at `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs` (shipped Pass #13) validates against `[A-Za-z0-9_.:/-]` and falls back to `stdin:parse:<uuid>` on charset fail; shell-side `cmd_rpc` (line ~489 of session.sh, shipped Pass #15) has no charset gate (unlike `cmd_send` line 390) and greps for `cid=stdin:req:<literal>` which never matches the uuid-scoped log line → post-hoc scan silently misses → generic timeout returned. Same failure shape as Pass #13's fixed `cmd_send --await-parse` issue but on the `rpc` path; Pass #13's fix added charset gate to `cmd_send` with unscoped-grep fallback, that pattern never carried to `cmd_rpc`. Positive controls from the same probe run: A1 (`requestId:"p16-A1"`), A2 (`a-b_c.d:e/f` — all charset members), B1-B5 (5 parallel malformed with distinct requestIds), C1-C4 (valid+malformed interleaved), D1-D2 (requestId reuse across malformed→valid respects `start_offset`), D3 (wrong `--expect` type with valid payload correctly returns generic timeout, scan does NOT falsely fire), E2 (backslash in `type` field escapes safely through `sed 's/\\/\\\\/g; s/"/\\"/g'`), E3 (500-char variant name serde error truncated to exactly 200 chars per `cut -c1-200`) all returned expected outcomes. Fix menu for a subsequent pass to pick from: (a) add charset gate to `cmd_rpc` shell side mirroring `cmd_send`'s line 390 pattern — fall back to unscoped grep on log tail when charset fails (least disruptive, shell-only change, structural parity with cmd_send). (b) broaden both-side charset to accept more chars (coordinated Rust+shell change, risks expanding attacker surface). (c) shift Rust to always emit `stdin:req:<extracted>` regardless of charset — forces shell to sanitize at grep input (drops Pass #13's shell-metachar defense). Preferred: (a). Acceptance: A3 + A5 replay return actionable `parse_error` envelopes with extracted serde error text.

Original Pass #8 history preserved below. --- Run 7 Pass #8 (2026-04-18T15:45Z) attacker-cadence probe — `triggerBuiltin` with an unknown `name` hits the catch-all `_ => logging::log("ERROR", &format!("Unknown built-in: '{}'", name))` arm at `src/main_entry/runtime_stdin_match_core.rs:318-320`, which echoes the FULL untrusted `name` payload verbatim into app.log at ERROR level. Evidence: 48-RPC, 6-category attacker probe (Rapid-fire 20× + Interrupted + Interleaved 8× + Boundary 6× + Concurrent 5× + Composition 5×) — 0 warn/error/panic lines for the 37 known-name calls, but 6 "Unknown built-in" ERROR lines for the 6 boundary cases. Of those, ONE 5000-char `x…` payload became a single ~5 100-byte log line (99% of the 5 383 bytes spent on that one call); empty, emoji (`🚀🔥`), zero-width-joiner (`\u200b\u200b\u200b`), RTL (`\u202e\u202eTEST`), and `totallyFakeBuiltin12345` all round-tripped their raw bytes into the log. Log-spam scales O(size_of_untrusted_input_per_call) — matches attacker-mode.md near-anomaly criterion "log spam scales with input size". Also a minor privacy/severity-level concern: an RPC no-op (silent fire-and-forget dispatch with the caller observing only a generic 2 s timeout) is being recorded at ERROR level rather than WARN/DEBUG, so ops dashboards and any "recent errors" grep will over-index on attacker-controlled strings. Fix menu: (a) length-cap the logged name at e.g. 120 chars with a `[truncated N bytes]` suffix — least invasive, preserves diagnostic value of the first few bytes (`&name[..name.len().min(120)]` with char-boundary care). (b) downgrade severity from ERROR to WARN (or DEBUG with structured `triggerBuiltin_unknown` event type) — matches the "defensive arm, not an error state" reality. (c) rate-limit duplicate unknown-name emissions in a sliding window. Preferred: (a)+(b) combined — cap AND downgrade; (c) is overkill for the threat model. Acceptance: replay the Pass #8 probe, observe no single log line > ~300 bytes for the unknown-name path AND the 6 unknown-name emissions appear at WARN (or structured DEBUG) rather than ERROR. Falsifier: any single `Unknown built-in:` log line exceeds 300 bytes OR the severity remains `|e|` (ERROR).
- [x] stdin-parse-externalcommand-field-error-masked-by-sdk-variant-list: Run 8 Pass #9 (2026-04-19T01:25Z) — **CLOSED by Prompt: Fix**. Adopted fix-menu options (a)+(d) combined at `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs::parse_stdin_command` — restructured `if let Ok(command) = from_value::<ExternalCommand>(...)` into `match { Ok(command) => return ..., Err(err) => err }` to capture the ExternalCommand error under `ext_err`, then introduced a short-circuit check: if `raw["type"].as_str()` matches a verb in `EXTERNAL_COMMAND_VERBS` (the existing const slice at `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs:696-723`), surface `anyhow::anyhow!("automation_payload_mismatch: \"{known_verb}\" is a known automation verb but the payload did not validate: {ext_err}")` instead of falling through to the Message fallback. Preserves the SDK Message fallback verbatim for truly unknown verbs so existing callers that pass raw prompt/response messages see no behavior change. Live receipts via `--await-parse` post-session-restart: (1) `{type:"setFilter",value:"foo"}` → `parseError: automation_payload_mismatch: "setFilter" is a known automation verb but the payload did not validate: unknown field \`value\`, expected \`text\` or \`requestId\``; (2) `{type:"setFilter"}` → `parseError: automation_payload_mismatch: "setFilter" is ... validate: missing field \`text\``; (3) `{type:"totallyFakeVerb","foo":"bar"}` → unchanged `parseError: unknown variant \`totallyFakeVerb\`, expected one of \`hello\`, \`helloAck\`, \`arg\`, \`div\`, \`submit\`, ...` (SDK fallback preserved); (4) `{type:"setFilter","text":"run"}` → `parseOutcome:"parsed", commandType:"setFilter"` (happy path unaffected). Three new unit tests pinned in `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs::tests`: `parse_stdin_command_surfaces_external_command_error_for_known_verb_with_wrong_field`, `parse_stdin_command_surfaces_external_command_error_for_missing_required_field`, `parse_stdin_command_unknown_type_still_uses_sdk_message_fallback` — all green. Falsifier: any future change that flips a reproducer from `automation_payload_mismatch` back to `unknown variant` text would break both the live receipt and the unit tests. Original `[?]` finding preserved below. --- Run 8 Pass #8 (2026-04-19T01:10Z) attacker-cadence probe — `bash scripts/agentic/session.sh rpc default '{"type":"setFilter","value":"foo"}'` (note wrong field name: automation uses `text`, not `value`) returns a `parse_error` whose message reads `unknown variant \`setFilter\`, expected one of \`hello\`, \`helloAck\`, \`arg\`, \`div\`, \`submit\`, \`update\`, \`exit\`, \`forceSubmit\`, \`setInput\`, \`editor\`, \`mini\`, \`micro\`, \`select\`, \`confirm\`, \`fields\`, \`form\`, …`. The listed variants are the SDK protocol `Message` enum (`src/protocol/message/variants/prompts_media.rs`), NOT the automation `ExternalCommand` enum that actually owns `setFilter` (`src/stdin_commands/mod.rs:664,700`). Root cause: `parse_stdin_command` at `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs:841-852` tries `ExternalCommand` first via `if let Ok(command) = serde_json::from_value::<ExternalCommand>(raw.clone())`, then UNCONDITIONALLY falls back to `serde_json::from_value::<crate::protocol::Message>(raw)?` and returns that error — discarding the ExternalCommand deserialize error even when the type field matches a known ExternalCommand variant. Evidence: three reproducer RPCs — `{type:"setFilter",value:"foo"}`, `{type:"setFilter"}` (missing `text`), `{type:"setFilter",value:"foo"}` with zalgo/RTL/emoji/2000-char payloads — all returned the identical misleading SDK-variant error text. Positive control: `{type:"setFilter",text:"run"}` (correct shape) reaches the automation dispatcher and returns a timeout (not a parse_error), confirming ExternalCommand DOES own `setFilter` when the payload validates. Impact: any automation-tool author debugging a typo (`value` vs `text`, or any deny_unknown_fields mismatch) is pointed at a totally different protocol vocabulary and concludes `setFilter` itself doesn't exist. The surfaced error lists `hello`, `arg`, `setInput`, `submit` — none of which are valid automation verbs. Cross-reference Pass #7 (Run 8) STEP-2 skip: the user's newly-committed additive `src/protocol/ingress.rs` (commit `66af39192`) is exactly the kind of structural observer that could be extended to fix this, but it's "not yet wired into `parse_message_graceful` or the stdin reader" per its module doc. Fix menu: (a) in `parse_stdin_command`, rename the discarded `ExternalCommand` error to `ext_err` and, if `raw["type"].as_str()` matches a known `ExternalCommand` variant name (enumerated by existing `KNOWN_COMMANDS` list at `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs:700`), surface `ext_err` instead of the Message fallback error — surgical, preserves the dual-dispatch order. (b) Present a composite "ExternalCommand: <err1> | Message: <err2>" error so both layers are visible regardless of which matched — extra noise but zero branching. (c) Reverse the dispatch order (Message first, ExternalCommand fallback) — rejected, same class of bug swapped. (d) Emit a distinct `parse_error` code like `automation_payload_mismatch` when the type matches `KNOWN_COMMANDS` but the payload fails — cleanest for programmatic consumers. Preferred: (a) + (d) combined. Acceptance: replay of `{type:"setFilter",value:"foo"}` returns a parse_error whose message contains `setFilter` AND names the missing/unexpected field (not the SDK variant list). Falsifier: the reproducer still lists `hello`, `arg`, `setInput` in the error text after the fix ships.

- [x] stdin-parse-dispatch-structural-pin-against-if-let-ok-collapse: Run 8 Pass #10 (2026-04-19T01:50Z) — **PIN**. Pass #9 (SHA `806db738e`) converted the ExternalCommand branch of `parse_stdin_command` from `if let Ok(command) = from_value(...)` to `let ext_err = match from_value::<ExternalCommand>(...) { Ok(command) => return ..., Err(err) => err }` and added an `EXTERNAL_COMMAND_VERBS.contains(t)` short-circuit that surfaces `automation_payload_mismatch: "<verb>" is a known automation verb but the payload did not validate: <serde-err>` before the SDK Message fallback. Pass #9 pinned the *output* via three behavioural unit tests; this pass pins the *structure* via a source-grep contract at `tests/stdin_parse_automation_payload_mismatch_contract.rs`. Three assertions fail loudly if a contributor "simplifies" the dispatch back to `if let Ok` (dropping `ext_err` and the `automation_payload_mismatch:` prefix): (1) body contains `let ext_err = match serde_json::from_value::<ExternalCommand>(`, (2) body contains `Err(err) => err,` (binding the error as a value, not `?` / `return Err(_)` / `panic!`), (3) body contains `EXTERNAL_COMMAND_VERBS.contains(` AND `automation_payload_mismatch:` literal. All three green on `cargo test -p script-kit-gpui --test stdin_parse_automation_payload_mismatch_contract` (3 passed, 40.1s compile + 0.00s run). Anchored on `parse_stdin_command_body()` which brace-counts the function body from `fn parse_stdin_command(` to its matching `}`, so renaming the function or splitting it will panic the tests with an actionable message ("function may have been renamed … Update anchors to match"). Behavioural regression coverage already exists in `src/stdin_commands/mod.rs::tests` (3 unit tests added by Pass #9); this structural contract is the belt to the behavioural suspenders — a refactor that preserves the 3 unit-test outputs via e.g. a manual re-parse inside `if let Ok`'s Err branch would still shift the structural contract and therefore still fail this contract. Falsifier: any commit that removes `let ext_err = match`, removes `Err(err) => err,`, or removes `EXTERNAL_COMMAND_VERBS.contains(` / `automation_payload_mismatch:` from `parse_stdin_command`'s body fails one or more of the 3 structural asserts. Surface: `tests/stdin_parse_automation_payload_mismatch_contract.rs` (new, distinct from Pass #9's in-module unit tests and the pre-existing `tests/stdin_parse_error_recovery_contract.rs` which pins the outer listener loop, not the parser function).

- [x] tool-panel-invariants-cold-start-race: Run 8 Pass #22 (2026-04-19T01:27Z) — **CLOSED by Prompt: Fix**. Root cause: the `post_make_key` phase asserted `[window isKeyWindow]` via `record` (fail-loud bucket) immediately after `[window makeKeyWindow]`. AppKit dispatches `makeKeyWindow` asynchronously on cold-start, so the observation races the promotion and returns false even though the launcher did everything right. With `record` wiring, a false observation pushed into `mismatched`, flipped `ok()`, and triggered the debug-build panic at `src/platform/panel_invariants.rs:326:13`. Fix: added a new `record_soft` method on `PanelInvariantReport` that targets a separate `soft_mismatched: Vec<Invariant>` bucket + a twin `log_soft_report` helper that emits `PANEL_INVARIANTS SOFT` lines; `finish()` calls it when `soft_mismatched` is non-empty but does NOT count soft failures toward `ok()`. Only the `is_key_window` check was migrated — all 11 other invariants (main_thread, main_window_registered, window_class, nonactivating_style, can_become_key, window_level, collection_behavior, activation_policy, animation_behavior, restorable, frame_autosave_name) read synchronously-configured state that cannot race and stay on fail-loud `record`. Existing `tests/panel_invariants_contract.rs` (6 tests) unaffected — all still green. cargo check clean. Live verification NOT performed: reproducing the race requires cold session restart, which would kill the running AFK session (pid 855) and abort the loop. The source-level correctness is grounded: the panic path is `finish()` → `panic!` gated on `!r.ok()`, and `r.ok()` returns `mismatched.is_empty()` which now excludes `is_key_window` entirely. A future pass that dedicates an explicit cold-restart slot can confirm the end-to-end disappearance of the panic. - [x] attacker-session-send-argorder-swallow: Run 8 Pass #21 (2026-04-19T01:17Z) — **CLOSED by Prompt: Fix**. Root cause reproduced by Pass #20 (commit `d3a15cefc`): `cmd_send` at `scripts/agentic/session.sh:276-281` unconditionally bound `local cmd="${2:-}"` — when invoked with flag-before-payload arg-order (`send SESSION --await-parse JSON`), `$2="--await-parse"` and the JSON was consumed by the flag-parse loop's `*) shift ;;` catch-all. Fix: added a shape-check guard directly after the `missing_command` check and BEFORE the FIFO write — `if [[ "$cmd" == --* ]]; then json_error "flag_as_command" "..."; return 1; fi`. Placement invariants pinned by 4 new asserts in `tests/session_send_await_parse_contract.rs::cmd_send_rejects_flag_as_command`: (a) guard literal `if [[ "$cmd" == --* ]]; then` present, (b) `json_error "flag_as_command"` literal present, (c) guard appears AFTER `json_error "missing_command"` (empty CMD still errors with `missing_command`, not `flag_as_command`), (d) guard appears BEFORE `printf '%s\n' "$cmd" > "$input_fifo"` (the FIFO never receives the flag string). All 8 tests in the contract file green (16.52s compile, 0.00s run — up from 7 to 8 tests). lat.md/automation.md §"Session send parse receipts" updated with a new paragraph documenting the `flag_as_command` stable-contract code alongside the existing `invalid_timeout` paragraph. Usage: ..."}}` ✓; (2) correct-order `send default '{...p21-correctorder...}' --await-parse` → `{schemaVersion:1, status:"ok", session:"default", sent:true, parseOutcome:"parsed", commandType:"getState"}` ✓ (proves the fix is surgical — didn't regress the correct path); (3) empty CMD `send default ''` → `{status:"error", error:{code:"missing_command", ...}}` ✓ (proves the guard didn't swallow the empty-CMD case). Falsifier: any commit that removes `if [[ "$cmd" == --* ]]` from session.sh, OR reorders so the guard runs AFTER the FIFO write, OR renames the error code from `flag_as_command` to anything else — all three would flip tests red. Adjacent DX win: this closes the client-side equivalent of Pass #9's server-side `automation_payload_mismatch` hole — Pass #9 gave the parser a clean field-level diagnostic when a known verb had a bad payload; this fix gives the SENDER a clean diagnostic when they typo the flag order. Original `[?]` prose preserved below for Run 8 Pass #20 attack context. --- Run 8 Pass #20 (2026-04-19T01:12Z) — attacker-cadence probe. `bash scripts/agentic/session.sh send SESSION --await-parse JSON` (flag BEFORE the JSON payload, arg-order typo that's easy to make) is silently swallowed. — attacker-cadence probe. `bash scripts/agentic/session.sh send SESSION --await-parse JSON` (flag BEFORE the JSON payload, arg-order typo that's easy to make) is silently swallowed. `cmd_send` at `scripts/agentic/session.sh:276-281` binds `local cmd="${2:-}"` unconditionally — when `$2="--await-parse"` the script writes the literal string `--await-parse\n` (13 bytes) to the input FIFO and returns `{schemaVersion:1, status:"ok", session:"...", sent:true}` (no `parseOutcome`, no warning). The stdin parser then emits `|w|S|cid=stdin:parse:<uuid> Failed to parse external command ... line_len=13 payload_summary={len:13} error=invalid number at line 1 column 2` (13 == `len("--await-parse")`). Six consecutive such parse_fails recorded in `/tmp/sk-agentic-sessions/default/app.log` this pass — exactly matching 6 wrong-order `send` invocations (A2 10k-char + A3-A7 boundary payloads). Control case `send SESSION JSON --await-parse` (correct order) returned `{..., sent:true, parseOutcome:"parsed", commandType:"getState"}` — proves the script is otherwise healthy. Fix menu: (a) guard `cmd_send` with a shape-check — if the first positional arg matches `^--` reject with `json_error "flag_as_command" "Did you mean: send SESSION JSON --flag? (got \`--await-parse\` as CMD)"`. (b) attempt a minimal JSON validation of `cmd` (`printf '%s' "$cmd" | head -c 1` must be `{`) and emit a warn-only envelope when it looks non-JSON. (c) bolster via a shell-level contract in `tests/session_send_await_parse_contract.rs` (existing file) that `send SESSION --await-parse JSON` returns `{status:"error", code:"flag_as_command"}` — pins the DX fix against regression. Preferred: (a) + (c) — (b) over-polices and would false-positive on any non-JSON cmd (which is not currently supported anyway). Acceptance: a fresh wrong-order invocation returns `status:"error" code:"flag_as_command"`; zero `stdin_parse_failed line_len=13` entries appear in app.log scoped to the request. Falsifier: any commit that removes the shape-check and restores silent swallow reverts this anomaly. Adversarial category fit: Boundary (flag-as-payload) + Composition (valid subcommand + valid flag in invalid order). Relation to Pass #9's `automation_payload_mismatch` surface: Pass #9 closed the server-side "known verb, bad payload" DX hole; this anomaly is the client-side equivalent — "bad invocation never reaches server as JSON".

Original Run 9 Pass #4 evidence preserved below. --- Run 9 Pass #4 (2026-04-19T05:35Z) — attacker-cadence probe. `rpc show` after a `hide` from any view restores the LAST-USED view rather than returning to a canonical "main menu" state. Scope caveat (why `[?]` not `[!]`): this may be intentional — "show the last window you saw" is a reasonable UX for a launcher bound to a global hotkey. But it's undocumented as a contract, and the automation receipts don't tell the caller which view they landed in without a follow-up `getState`. Adversarial category fit: Composition (hide + show without triggerBuiltin) + Resurrection (show restores a view that was dismissed) + Boundary (response-envelope shape — show emits no matching-requestId echo, callers discover state only via getState).

- [x] attacker-stdin-requestid-nul-newline-match-loss: Run 9 Pass #1 (2026-04-19T04:51Z) — CLOSED by Extend. Acceptance option (a) shipped — added sender-side `invalid_request_id_charset` gate in `scripts/agentic/session.sh::cmd_rpc` that rejects requestIds containing a literal backslash OR `[[:cntrl:]]` chars BEFORE FIFO write. Live verification on session pid 35219: `requestId:"with\u0000nul"` → rejected in 0.011s with `code:"invalid_request_id_charset"` (was 2000ms timeout); `requestId:"line1\nline2"` → same 0.009s reject; normal `requestId:"run9-p1-smoke"` → `status:"ok" responseType:"stateResult"` unchanged. Original Run 8 Pass #24 evidence — attacker-cadence probe. `requestId` containing `\u0000` (NUL) or `\n` (literal newline serialized as JSON `\n` escape) sends cleanly but no response can be matched downstream. Evidence: A04 `{"type":"getState","requestId":"with\u0000nul"}` → `code:"timeout", message:"No response matching requestId 'with\\u0000nul' within 2000ms"`; A05 `{"type":"getState","requestId":"line1\nline2"}` → `code:"timeout", message:"No response matching requestId 'line1\\nline2'"`. Unknown whether (a) the stdin parser rejects the command silently, (b) the app produces a response with a different-encoded requestId (e.g. normalized), or (c) the `responses.ndjson` tail+jq match-loop in `cmd_rpc` fails to correlate because of the embedded special char. App did NOT switch view — follow-up getState showed steady-state — so either (a) or (c). Distinct from `attacker-stdin-requestid-unbounded` (length boundary works; this is a character-class boundary). Scope caveat (why `[?]` not `[!]`): these are caller-supplied correlation ids, and NUL/newline in a correlation id is almost certainly a caller bug — but the SYMPTOM (silent timeout, caller never learns whether the app processed) mirrors the `attacker-session-send-argorder-swallow` DX class closed Run 8 Pass #21. Acceptance: either (a) add a sender-side validation in `cmd_rpc` that rejects requestIds containing control chars (`[\x00-\x1f]`) with `invalid_request_id_charset` before writing to FIFO, OR (b) document the charset contract in lat.md/automation.md §"Session send parse receipts" so callers know to restrict to `[A-Za-z0-9_.:/-]+` (matches the existing `stdin_commands::mod.rs::extract_request_id_lenient` charset). Falsifier: any receipt where a requestId containing `\u0000` or `\n` produces a non-timeout match. Adversarial category fit: Boundary (control chars) + Composition (valid verb + control-char correlation id) + Race (the timeout hides whether it's a parse-level drop or a match-level drop — two distinct failure modes collapsed to one observable).

- [ ] stdin-requestid-boundary-rpc-correlation: Charset-safe and charset-unsafe requestIds plus concurrent malformed payloads each produce correct parse receipts with no cross-correlation; prefix-matching requestIds do not collide.

- [ ] escalated-attacker-cross-surface-lifecycle: First attacker slot of Run 10 — ≥30 actions, ≥4 surfaces, ≥4 adversarial categories, ≥1 out-of-bounds payload. File `[?]` for any near-anomaly; fix in a later pass, not this one. Escalation required by Run 9 scheduler-stop note (3 consecutive zero-`[?]` attacker passes).
- [x] validate-amount-accepts-nan-inf-as-numeric: Run 11 Pass #26 (commit `d43eca4f3`) — FIXED. `looks_like_amount` now requires `is_finite()` after `parse::<f64>()`, so `NaN`/`nan`/`inf`/`-inf`/`infinity`/`+infinity`/`Infinity` all return false → `validate` short-circuits with `Malformed { field: Kv("amount"), reason: "amount must be numeric, got `NaN`" }`. Pinned by `validate_amount_rejects_nan_and_infinity` (capture_schema lib) and the converted Pass-16 attacker probes `boundary_09_amount_NaN_is_malformed_PINNED` + `boundary_10_amount_inf_is_malformed_PINNED`. Existing `validate_amount_accepts_decimals_and_signs` continues to pass for `"18.50"`/`"$18.50"`/`"-5"`/`"+12.0"`/`"0"`/`"100"` — falsifier confirms the tightening did not over-reject.
- [x] validate-ignores-schema-forbidden-fields: Run 11 Pass #26 (commit `d43eca4f3`) — FIXED. `validate` now sweeps `schema.forbidden` after the kv-amount well-formedness loop and before `missing_required`. Any forbidden field whose `is_satisfied(payload)` returns true short-circuits with `Malformed { field, reason: format!("{label} is not allowed for +{target}") }`. Pinned by `validate_malformed_when_forbidden_field_present` (priority on +cal even with all required satisfied), `validate_forbidden_url_on_cal_beats_incomplete` (precedence over Incomplete), and `validate_ready_unaffected_when_no_forbidden_fields_set` (the falsifier — defensive: a +cal payload using none of the forbidden fields still validates Ready). The Pass-16 attacker probe `composition_18_forbidden_field_is_malformed_PINNED` (converted from `_PROBE`) covers the same surface from the integration-test side. `validate_ready_when_all_required_present_and_well_formed` (Pass 15 test) continues to pass — confirms no regression.
- [x] skill-spec-family-filter-case-sensitive: Run 11 Pass #30 (commit `191147353`) — FIXED. Family check uses `eq_ignore_ascii_case("skill.v1")` so `SKILL.V1`/`Skill.V1`/`sKiLl.v1` etc. all extract cleanly. Pinned by lib `family_match_is_case_insensitive` (5 spellings + falsifier `skill.v11` typo) and converted attacker `boundary_10_uppercase_family_matches_case_insensitively_PINNED`. Original probe: Run 11 Pass #20 (commit `b47bd544f`). [[src/menu_syntax/skill.rs#skill_specs_from_value]] compares `family` against the literal `"skill.v1"` (case-sensitive). Other modules in the codebase normalize case before comparison (e.g. `command_head_matches`, `builtin_schema` lowercase first). An author writing `"SKILL.V1"` (capitalization mistake, autocorrect, copy-paste from a doc that title-cased) gets silent filter-out — the skill registration vanishes with no warning. Fix shape (deferred): change the family check to `obj.get("family").and_then(|v| v.as_str()).map(|s| s.eq_ignore_ascii_case("skill.v1")) == Some(true)`. Add a Pass 20 attacker fixture (`boundary_10_uppercase_family_is_filtered_PROBE`) that flips from `is_empty()` → `len() == 1`. Falsifier once fixed: lowercase `"skill.v1"` still extracts cleanly.
- [x] skill-spec-no-dedup-on-duplicate-slugs: Run 11 Pass #30 (commit `191147353`) — FIXED. After the extraction loop, `skill_specs_from_value` runs `out.retain(...)` keyed on `slug`, keeping the FIRST occurrence (declaration-order wins). Pinned by lib `duplicate_slugs_are_deduped_keeping_first` (asserts `specs[0].label == Some("First")`), `dedup_preserves_distinct_slugs` (3 distinct slugs all surface — falsifier for over-dedup), `dedup_treats_trimmed_slug_as_same` (whitespace-padded duplicate collapses), and converted attacker `composition_11_duplicate_slugs_dedupe_first_wins_PINNED`. Original probe: Run 11 Pass #20 (commit `b47bd544f`). [[src/menu_syntax/skill.rs#skill_specs_from_value]] does not dedupe by slug. Two `{ family: "skill.v1", slug: "review" }` entries surface as two SkillSpecs in the returned Vec. The runtime `:type:skill review` filter would render them as two visually-identical rows (or two slightly-different rows if labels differ). Either is confusing. Fix shape (deferred): after the loop, dedupe by `slug` keeping the LAST occurrence (so a more specific override wins) OR keep the FIRST occurrence (declaration-order wins). Pick one and document. Falsifier once fixed: `composition_11_duplicate_slugs_both_surface_PROBE` flips from `len() == 2` to `len() == 1`. Adjacent decision: same script declaring `{family:"skill.v1",slug:"a"}` and `{family:"skill.v1",slug:"a"}` is malformed-author behavior; `doctor.rs` should also flag it as a Warning during the same fix pass.

- [x] dynamic-schema-no-dedup-across-required-optional: Run 11 Pass #33 (commit `88fa14985`) — FIXED. [[src/menu_syntax/metadata.rs#dynamic_capture_schema_from_spec]] now runs a two-phase dedup. Phase 1 (within-list): the `parse_list` closure collects parsed `FieldRequirement`s into a `Vec`, skipping any value that already appears (`if !out.contains(&req) { out.push(req); }`) — so three identical `body` tokens collapse to a single `FieldRequirement::Body` and a 50-entry `kv:k` list collapses to one. Phase 2 (cross-list precedence): `optional.retain(|r| !required.contains(r))` and `forbidden.retain(|r| !required.contains(r) && !optional.contains(r))` — `required > optional > forbidden`. Pinned by Pass 24 attacker tests (originally `composition_14_duplicate_required_tokens_preserved_PROBE` + `composition_17_long_required_list_handled` + `resurrection_23_kv_in_both_required_and_optional_no_dedup`) all converted in-place to `_PINNED` with inverted assertions, plus three new pins: `composition_14b_cross_list_required_wins_over_optional_and_forbidden_PINNED` (kv:amount in all three lists → only required), `composition_14c_optional_wins_over_forbidden_when_required_silent_PINNED`, and `composition_14d_distinct_fields_across_lists_all_survive_PINNED` (over-dedup falsifier). 27 attacker tests + 20 lib tests pass. Adjacent: `doctor.rs` should still warn about cross-list duplicates as an authoring smell — that's a future Add for the doctor surface, not blocking this Fix. Original probe: Run 11 Pass #24 (commit `7d3d4831c`).

[[src/app_impl/menu_syntax_ai_apply.rs#apply_proposal]]'s `AddDate` arm now does `format!("{key}:{}", quote_for_filter_value(phrase))`. Pass-36 attacker test `boundary_05_..._produces_unbalanced_output` converted in-place to `boundary_05_..._is_backslash_escaped_PINNED` with inverted assertion (`due:"today \"9am\""` instead of `due:"today "9am""`) plus a falsifier guard counting unescaped `"` chars (must be exactly 2). `boundary_06_..._passes_through_unescaped` also converted to `_is_doubled_PINNED` since `\` now escapes too. Original probe: Pass #36 (commit `2a5ffae56`). Sister fix in same commit: `action-effects-default-time-phrase-not-quote-escaped` (Pass-32 `[?]`). Adjacent gap NOT addressed in this Fix: `AddField { key, value }` still does not quote `value` (`format!("{key}={value}")`); `value` vocabulary is more constrained (primitives) so the surface area is smaller — left for a future probe.
- [x] action-effects-default-time-phrase-not-quote-escaped: Run 11 Pass #41 (commit `284edbbd7`) — FIXED via shared helper [[src/menu_syntax/quote.rs#quote_for_filter_value]] (joint fix with `ai-apply-add-date-phrase-not-quote-escaped`). [[src/menu_syntax/action_effects.rs#apply_safe_effect]]'s `DefaultTime` arm now does `format!("{trimmed} start:{}", quote_for_filter_value(phrase))` instead of `format!("{trimmed} start:\"{phrase}\"")`. Existing tests using clean phrases (`today 9am` etc.) keep passing because the helper is a pass-through for non-quote/non-backslash content.
